<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chester_A._Arthur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some older sources list the date as October&#160;5, 1830,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHowe5_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHowe5-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> but biographer <a href="/wiki/Thomas_C._Reeves" title="Thomas C. Reeves">Thomas C. Reeves</a> confirms that this is incorrect: Arthur claimed to be a year younger "out of simple vanity."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves19755_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves19755-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Arthur pronounced his middle name with the accent on the second syllable.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves19755_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves19755-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Twelfth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Twelfth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Twelfth Amendment to the United States Constitution</a> applies that clause, which specifically restricts presidential eligibility, to would-be vice presidents, as well: "no person constitutionally ineligible to the office of President shall be eligible to that of Vice-President".</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">$10,000 in 1870 is equal to $187&#160;thousand in present terms.<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-US_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-US-50"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-59">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">$50,000 in 1871 is equal to $984&#160;thousand in present terms.<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-US_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-US-50"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-80">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Charles_K._Graham" title="Charles K. Graham">Charles K. Graham</a> filled Merritt's former position.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom370_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoogenboom370-79"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-95">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Biographer George Howe takes this exchange at face value,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHowe109_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHowe109-93"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> but later biographers suspect it may be apocryphal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1975179Karabell40.E2.80.9341_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1975179Karabell40.E2.80.9341-94"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-110">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Before the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Seventeenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Seventeenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Seventeenth Amendment to the United States Constitution</a>, Senators were elected by state legislatures.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Conkling and Pratt were ultimately denied re-election, being succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Elbridge_G._Lapham" title="Elbridge G. Lapham">Elbridge G. Lapham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warner_Miller" title="Warner Miller">Warner Miller</a>, respectively.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-148"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-148">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The portion of the law denying citizenship to Chinese-Americans was later found unconstitutional in <i><a href="/wiki/United_States_v._Wong_Kim_Ark" title="United States v. Wong Kim Ark">United States v. Wong Kim Ark</a></i> in 1898.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-181"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-181">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A small number of Arthur's papers survived and passed to his grandson, <a href="/wiki/Gavin_Arthur" title="Gavin Arthur">Gavin Arthur</a> (born Chester Alan Arthur III,) who allowed Arthur's biographer, Thomas C. Reeves, to examine them the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1972.27.27passim.27.27_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1972.27.27passim.27.27-180"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>
